Tadbir of the Fetus and Its Effect on the Mother's Transfer
Rulings on tadbir of fetus and effect on mother's transfer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on tadbir of the fetus and explain how it affects the permissibility of selling or gifting the mother, including the intra-Hanafi difference on gifting after tadbir.

Core Idea
Emancipating the fetus prohibits selling the mother but permits gifting; tadbir alone also restricts gifting.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq discusses the validity of making a fetus a mudabbar and the resulting limitations on transferring the mother. The key distinction is between sale (which separates the free child) and gift (which keeps them together). The author also explores the general principle that a child follows the mother in legal status, and includes an intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether gifting the mother after tadbir is allowed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the legal status of making the fetus a mudabbar? The author indicates it is valid a fortiori. Also, note the ruling on selling the mother after fully emancipating the fetus.
Tadbir is a declaration that the slave will be free after the master's death.
2
Distinguish between sale and gift
After emancipation of the fetus, selling the mother is not permissible because it would separate the free child from the mother. However, gifting her is permissible because the child remains with her. Understand the reasoning: the prohibition of separation (tafriq) applies to sale but not gift.
The text also mentions that if the fetus is only mudabbar (not fully emancipated), gifting the mother is not permissible according to al-Mabsut.
3
Examine the conditions for invalidating the sale
The sale of the mother is not invalidated immediately; it only becomes invalid if the child is born within six months, proving the fetus was already free at the time of sale.
This is to avoid uncertainty: the emancipation might not have taken effect if the child is not born.
4
Apply the general principle: al-walad yatba' al-umm
The child follows the mother in matters of ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad, and kitabah. This is based on consensus and the reasoning that the child is formed from the mother's menses.
This principle also applies to animals, but with exceptions as noted in the text (e.g., offspring of a dog and sheep).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأشار المصنف إلى أن تدبير الحمل وحده صحيح بالأولى قالوا ولا يجوز بيع الأم إذا أعتق ما في بطنها ويجوز هبتها والفرق أن استثناء ما في بطنها عند بيعها لا يجوز قصداً فكذا حكماً بخلاف الهبة لكن لا يحكم ببطلان البيع إلا بعد الولادة لأقل من ستة أشهر، وفي المبسوط : دبر ما في البطن لو وهب الأم لا يجوز وهو الأصح والفرق أن بالتدبير لا يزول ملكه عما في البطن فإذا وهب الأم بعد التدبير فالموهوب متصل بما ليس بموهوب فيكون في معنى هبة المشاع فيما يحتمل القسمة، وأما بعد العتق ما في البطن غير مملوك اهـ. وفي المحيط: لو قال لأمته أنت حرة أو ما في بطنك عتقت إذا لم تكن حاملاً لأن التخيير لم يصح، ولو قال لأمته الحامل أنت حرة أو ما في بطنك حر فضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت جنيناً ميتاً قد استبان خلقه قال يخير المولى؛ فإن أوقع العتق على الأم عتق الجنين بعتقها وعلى الضارب غرة للمولى، وإن مات المولى قبل البيان فضرب إنسان بطنها فألقت جنيناً ميتاً قد استبان خلقه قال في الجنين غرة حر ويعتق نصف الأمة وتسعى في نصف قيمتها ولا سعاية على الجنين اهـ. وفي الظهيرية : رجل أوصى بما في بطن جاريته لإنسان فمات الموصي فأعتق الورثة ما في بطن الجارية جاز إعتاقهم ويضمنون قيمة الولد الولادة . قوله : ( والولد يتبع الأم في الملك والحرية والرق والتدبير والاستيلاد والكتابة) لإجماع الأمة ولأن ماءه يكون مستهلكاً بمائها فيرجح جانبها، ولأنه متيقن به من جهتها ولهذا يثبت يوم قوله : ( فاعتق الورثة ما في بطن الجارية) كذا رأيته في الظهيرية. وفي كافي الحاكم : فأعتق الوارث الأمة فهو جائز وولاؤها وولاء ما في بطنها له وهو ضامن لقيمة ما في بطنها يوم تلد قوله : (وكذا يعتبر جانب الأم في البهائم) قال الرملي : هذا منقوض بالشاة إذا نزا عليها كلب فولدت فإنه لا تجوز التضحية به عند عامة العلماء كما ذكره في البزازية وغيرها .اهـ. قلت: لكن في الوهبانية : وإن ينز كلب فوق عنز فجاءت نتاج له رأس الكلاب فينظر فإن أكلت لحماً فكلب جميعها وإن أكلت تبـنـاً فـذا الرأس يـبـتـر ويؤكل باقيها وإن أكلت لذا وذا فاضربـنـهـا فـالـصــيــاح يخبر وإن أشكلت فاذبح فإن كرشها بدا فعنز وإلا فهي كلب فيطمر قال شارحها الشرنبلالي المسألة من الظهيرية : كلب نزا على عنز فولدت ولداً رأسه رأس كلب
And the author indicated that tadbir of the fetus alone is valid a fortiori. They said: it is not permissible to sell the mother if he has emancipated what is in her womb, but it is permissible to gift her. The difference is that exempting what is in her womb at the time of selling is not permissible intentionally, so likewise legally; unlike gift. However, the sale is not ruled invalid except after birth at less than six months. And in al-Mabsut: if he makes a mudabbar of what is in the womb and then gifts the mother, it is not permissible, and that is the more correct view. The difference is that by tadbir his ownership of what is in the womb does not cease, so if he gifts the mother after tadbir, the gifted is connected to what is not gifted, thus it is like gifting joint property in what is divisible. As for after emancipation, what is in the womb is no longer owned. And in al-Muhit: if he said to his slave-girl 'you are free or what is in your womb is free', it becomes free if she is not pregnant because the choice did not take effect. And if he said to his pregnant slave-girl 'you are free or what is in your womb is free', and then a person struck her belly and she miscarried a dead fetus whose limbs had become apparent, he said: the master is given the choice. If he places the emancipation on the mother, the fetus becomes free by her emancipation, and the striker owes a ghurrah to the master. And if the master dies before the declaration, and a person struck her belly and she miscarried a dead fetus whose limbs had become apparent, concerning the fetus there is a ghurrah of a free person, and half of the slave-girl is emancipated, and she must work to pay half her value, and there is no earning obligation on the fetus. And in al-Zahiriyya: a man bequeathed what is in his slave-girl's womb to a person, then the testator died, and the heirs emancipated what is in the slave-girl's womb. Their emancipation is valid, and they are liable for the value of the child at birth. His statement: (and the child follows the mother in ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad, and kitabah) due to the consensus of the ummah, and because his water (semen) is consumed in her water, so her side predominates, and because he is certain from her side, and for this reason it is established on the day of his statement: (so the heirs emancipated what is in the slave-girl's womb) thus I saw it in al-Zahiriyya. And in Kafi al-Hakim: so the heir emancipated the slave-girl, it is permissible, and her wala' and the wala' of what is in her womb belong to him, and he is liable for the value of what is in her womb on the day she gives birth. His statement: (and similarly the mother's side is considered in animals). Al-Ramli said: this is contradicted by the case of a sheep which a dog mounts and then gives birth; it is not permissible for sacrifice according to most scholars, as mentioned in al-Bazzaziyya and others. I (the author) say: but in al-Wahbaniyya: if a dog mounts a goat and its offspring has a dog's head, then look: if it eats meat, it is all dog; if it eats straw, that head is cut off and the rest is eaten; if it eats both, then strike it and the screaming tells; if unclear, slaughter: if its stomach shows, it is a goat, otherwise it is a dog and is buried. The commentator al-Shurunbulali said: the issue is from al-Zahiriyya: a dog mounted a goat and gave birth to an offspring with a dog's head.
Source pages p. 392

Commentary
This passage covers multiple rulings on the legal status of the fetus after emancipation or tadbir, and the effect on the mother. The author (al-Musannif) indicates that making the fetus a mudabbar (i.e., declaring it free upon the master's death) alone is valid. After the fetus is emancipated, the mother cannot be sold because that would implicitly separate the free child from the mother, which is impermissible; but she can be gifted because the child will remain with her. However, the sale is only invalidated if the child is born within six months (proving the emancipation took effect). Al-Mabsut adds that if the fetus is only mudabbar, gifting the mother is not permissible because the connection remains. Then the text presents a case from al-Muhit: if the master gives an option to the mother: 'you are free or what is in your womb is free', and she is pregnant, the master has the choice to apply the emancipation to either. If he chooses the mother, the fetus becomes free by her freedom; if an outsider strikes and causes miscarriage, the striker owes a ghurrah to the master. If the master dies before choosing, and then the mother is struck and miscarries, half of the mother becomes free (due to inheritance? actually: the option passes to the heirs?), and the fetus gets a ghurrah, and the mother must work to pay half her value. Then the text addresses bequest of the fetus: if a man bequeaths the fetus to someone, and the heirs emancipate it, it is valid, and the heirs owe its value. The passage concludes with the general principle: the child follows the mother in matters of ownership, freedom, slavery, tadbir, istilad (giving birth to a child of the master), and kitabah (contract of emancipation). This is because the child is formed from the mother's menses, and the father's semen is considered consumed. Finally, an aside: in animals, the mother's side also determines the offspring's status, but al-Ramli notes an exception: if a dog mounts a sheep, the offspring cannot be sacrificed (e.g., for Eid). The author cites al-Wahbaniyya with a practical rule for distinguishing: if the offspring eats meat, it is a dog; if only straw, the dog-like head is cut off and the rest is halal; if both, then use the stomach as a sign.

Key Terms
تدبير الحمل (tadbir al-haml): Declaring the fetus free upon the master's death; valid alone according to the author.
الولد يتبع الأم (al-walad yatba' al-umm): The child follows the mother in legal attributes (freedom, slavery, etc.)
غرة (ghurrah): Compensation for a fetus miscarried due to injury, often a fixed amount or a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on selling a mother slave after the fetus in her womb has been fully emancipated (i.e., made free)?
A) It is valid because the fetus is free and separate.
B) It is not permissible because it would separate the free child from the mother.
C) It is only permissible if the child is born alive.
D) It is permissible only if the buyer agrees to keep them together.

Key Takeaway
Tadbir of the fetus is valid; full emancipation prohibits sale of the mother, while tadbir alone restricts gifting—reflecting the principle that the child follows the mother and the prohibition of separating mother and child.

The Principle of Taba'iyyah: Child Follows Mother in Status
Establishes the principle of taba'iyyah with qiyas and applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi principle that the unborn child follows the mother in legal attributes (freedom, slavery, edibility) and apply the qiyas that the child is like a limb of the mother to derive rulings.

Core Idea
The unborn child is like a limb of the mother – its status follows hers until birth.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a foundational principle in Hanafi fiqh: the legal dependency (taba'iyyah) of the unborn child on the mother. The author draws an analogy: before birth, the child is like a part of the mother's body, sharing her nourishment and her legal status. Therefore, whatever ruling applies to the mother—freedom, slavery, edibility—extends to the child during pregnancy. The text then clarifies that this dependency ends at birth, and presents several related cases including disputes over timing of emancipation or tadbir, as well as an interesting scenario where a child can be born free from two slave parents.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal principle
State the principle: The unborn child (haml) follows the mother in freedom, slavery, and other attributes because it is considered part of her before birth.
The text explicitly says it is like a limb (ka-'udw).
2
Examine the qiyas
Analyze the analogy: the child is like a limb of the mother both physically (nourished by her) and legally (enters into transactions dependent on her). This makes the mother's side stronger, so the child's status mirrors hers.
This is a clear qiyas jaliy (clear analogy).
3
Apply the principle to animals
Extend the principle to animals: if a hybrid is born, the mother's edibility and suitability for sacrifice determine the offspring's ruling.
The text gives examples of wild/domestic and edible/inedible crossings.
4
Distinguish before and after birth
Note that the principle only applies during pregnancy. After birth, the child is independent and does not automatically follow the mother's later changes in status (e.g., if the mother is emancipated after birth, the child remains a slave).
The author prefers terms 'haml' (pregnancy) or 'janin' (fetus) over 'walad' (child) to emphasize this.
5
Handle disputes about timing
In cases where the master and mother disagree about whether the child was born before or after emancipation or tadbir, the ruling depends on possession and evidence: the child's location and who brings proof determine the outcome.
The text details various scenarios for mudabbara, mu'taqa, and kitaba, with a special rule if the child can speak for itself.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو حر أعضائها نسب ولد الزنا ولد الملاعنة منها حتى ترثه ويرثها لأنه قبل الانفصال هو كعضو من حساً وحكماً حتى يتغذى بغذائها، ويدخل في البيع والعتق وغيرهما من التصرفات تبعاً لها فكان جانبها أرجح. وكذا يعتبر جانب الأم في البهائم أيضاً حتى إذا تولد بين الوحشي والأهلي المأكول وغير المأكول يؤكل إذا كانت أمه مأكولة، وتجوز الأضحية به إذا كانت أمه يجوز بين التضحية بها. وفي الظهيرية : لو قال القائل هل يصير الولد حراً من زوجين رقيقين من غير إعتاق ولا وصية ؟ قيل : نعم وصورته إذا كان للحر ولد هو عبد الأجنبي فزوج الأب جاريته من ولده برضا مولاه فولدت الجارية ولداً فهو لأنه ولد ولد المولى . ولو عبر المصنف بالحمل أو بالجنين بدل الولد لكان أولى لأنه لا يتبع الأم في أوصافها إلا الحمل، وأما الولد بعد الوضع فلا يتبعها في شيء مما ذكر حتى لو أعتق الأم بعد الولادة لا يعتق الولد، وقد علمت مما قدمناه أن المراد بالحرية هنا الحرية الأصلية، وأما الطارئة فقد أفادها أولاً بقوله «ولو أعتق حاملاً عتقاً. وفي البدائع : لو اختلف المولى والمدبرة في ولدها فقال المولى ولدتيه قبل التدبير فهو رقيق ولدته بعده فهو مدبر فالقول قول المولى مع يمينه على علمه والبينة بينة المدبرة. ولو كان مكان التدبير عتق فقال المولى للمعتقة ولدتيه قبل العتق وهو رقيق وقالت ولدته بعد العتق وهو حر يحكم فيه الحال إن كان الولد في يدها فالقول قولها وإن كان في يد المولى فالقول قوله لأن الظاهر يشهد لمن هو في يده بخلاف المدبرة فإنها في يد المولى فكذا ولدها اهـ. وفي الخانية من الدعوى في مسألة إعتاقها : لو كان الولد في أيديهما فكذلك يكون القول قولها لأنها تدعي الولادة في أقرب الأوقات وفيه حرية الولد ولو أقاما البينة فبينتها أولى لأن بينة المولى قامت على نفي العتق وبينتها قامت على إثبات الحرية وكذلك في الكتابة، وأما في التدبير فالقول قول المولى لأنهما تصادقا على رق .الولد. وذكر في المنتقى عن محمد: إن كان الولد يعبر عن نفسه يرجع إليه ويكون القول للولد وإلا فالقول لمن هو في يده منهما اهـ . وقالت هي
Or free is her organs lineage of the child of adultery, child of imprecation from her so that she inherits from him and he inherits from her because before separation it is like a limb from her physically and legally, so it is nourished by her nourishment, and enters into sale, emancipation, and other dispositions as dependent on her, so her side was stronger. Likewise the mother's side is considered in animals too, so if a hybrid is born between wild and domestic, edible and inedible, it is eaten if its mother is edible, and it is permissible to sacrifice with it if its mother is permissible for sacrifice. And in al-Zahiriyya: if someone says: Can a child become free from two slave parents without emancipation or will? It was said: Yes, and its form is if a free man has a son who is the slave of another, then the father marries his female slave to his son with the permission of his master, then the female slave gives birth to a child, then he is the child of the child of the master. And if the author expressed 'pregnancy' or 'fetus' instead of 'child', it would be better because it does not follow the mother in her attributes except during pregnancy; as for the child after birth, it does not follow her in any of what was mentioned, even if he emancipates the mother after birth, the child is not emancipated. And you have known from what we have presented that by freedom here is meant original freedom; as for accidental freedom, he indicated it earlier by his saying: 'if he emancipated a pregnant woman, both are emancipated.' And if instead of tadbir there was emancipation, and the master says to the mu'taqa: you gave birth to him before emancipation and he is a slave, and she says: after emancipation and he is free, then the ruling is according to the situation: if the child is in her hand, the statement is hers; if in the master's hand, the statement is his, because the apparent evidence supports whoever has it in his hand, contrary to the mudabbara, because she is in the master's hand, and likewise her child. And in al-Khaniyya from al-Da'wa in the issue of her emancipation: if the child is in both their hands, then likewise the statement is hers because she claims birth in the nearest time and in it is the freedom of the child; and if both bring evidence, her evidence is stronger because the master's evidence came to negate emancipation and her evidence came to prove freedom, and similarly in kitaba; as for tadbir, the statement is the master's because they agreed upon the slavery of the child. And it is mentioned in al-Muntaqa from Muhammad: if the child can express himself, then it is referred to him and the statement is the child's; otherwise, the statement is for whoever of them has him in his hand. And she said.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a ruling establishing the principle of taba'iyyah (dependency) of the child upon the mother during pregnancy. The author explains that before birth, the child is considered a part of the mother both physically and legally, so it shares her status regarding freedom, slavery, and other attributes like edibility and suitability for sacrifice. This principle is extended to animals as well. The passage then presents specific cases: a child can be born free from two slave parents under special conditions (when the father is the slave's child and the mother is the master's slave), and disputes about the timing of birth relative to emancipation or tadbir are resolved by considering possession and evidence. The key nuance is that this dependency only applies to the unborn child (haml); once born, the child does not automatically follow the mother's later changes in status. The text also distinguishes between original and accidental freedom.

Key Terms
التابعية (al-tābi‘iyyah): The legal principle that the unborn child follows the mother in status because it is considered part of her before birth.
الحرية الأصلية (al-ḥurriyyah al-aṣliyyah): Original freedom, as opposed to accidental freedom gained through emancipation.
المدبرة (al-mudabbara): A female slave who has been promised freedom upon her master's death (tadbir).
المعتقة (al-mu‘taqa): A female slave who has been emancipated (set free).
الكتابة (al-kitāba): A contract of manumission where the slave pays for freedom in installments.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a master emancipates a pregnant slave woman, what is the status of her child according to the passage?
A) The child is free because it follows the mother's freedom at conception.
B) The child is free because it follows the mother's freedom at birth.
C) The child is a slave because it was conceived while the mother was a slave.
D) The child is free only if the master explicitly includes it in the emancipation.

Key Takeaway
The unborn child is legally part of the mother; thus its status reflects hers until birth, after which it becomes independent.

Distinction Between Raqq and Milk: Definitions and Legal Implications
Defines raqq and milk and their legal distinction

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define raqq and milk, explain their distinction, and apply the Hanafi framework to determine the permissibility of sale, intercourse, and expiation for different slave categories.

Core Idea
Raqq is a legal incapacity; milk is the power to dispose; their combination determines key rulings.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah explains the fundamental distinction between raqq (legal slavery) and milk (ownership). Though often conflated, these are two distinct legal statuses that interact in predictable ways. The passage also explores the nature of raqq—whether it is a right of Allah or of the public—and then applies the distinction to various slave categories. Mastering this framework is essential for understanding Hanafi rulings on transactions, family relations, and expiation.

Guided Path
1
Define milk and raqq
Identify the core definitions: milk is the initial power to dispose (tasarruf) over property or persons; raqq is a legal incapacity that prevents a person from exercising guardianship, testimony, judgment, and full ownership. Note that milk is active, while raqq is passive.
Milk exists in inanimate objects and animals; raqq only applies to humans.
2
Analyze how sale and emancipation affect each
The passage explicitly states: sale removes milk but not raqq; emancipation removes milk intentionally (as a right of the owner) and raqq implicitly (since the slave becomes free). Understand that milk is a transferable right, while raqq is a status that is only removed through liberation.
Emancipation does not target raqq directly; it becomes empty of the owner's rights.
3
Evaluate the dispute over raqq's nature
Some Hanafi scholars say raqq is a right of Allah because it arose from disbelief (the cause of slavery). Others say it is a right of the public (general welfare) because it serves societal interests. This dispute affects whether raqq can be waived, but the practical rulings are unaffected.
The text does not settle on one view; both are presented.
4
Apply the distinction to slave categories
For qinn (full slave): both milk and raqq are complete → sale and expiation valid. For umm walad and mudabbar: raqq deficient but milk complete → cannot be used for expiation, but intercourse allowed. For mukatab: raqq complete but milk deficient → expiation valid, but cannot be sold (milk deficient).
The text summarizes: sale depends on completeness of both, intercourse on milk only, expiation on raqq only.
5
Identify the exception for lineage and religion
Lineage follows the father, slavery follows the mother—except when the father is deceived (mugharrar), then the child is free. Religion follows the better of the two parents. This clarifies that slavery status is inherited from the mother unless the father was unaware of her slavery.
The mugharrar exception is detailed in later chapters.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أشار المصنف بعطف الرق على الملك إلى المغايرة بينهما وهو " كذلك فإن الملك هو القدرة على التصرف ابتداء فخرج الولي والوصي والوكيل وأما الرق فعجز حكمي عن الولاية والشهادة والقضاء ومالكية المال كائن عن جعله شرعاً عرضة للتملك والابتذال . واختلفوا هل هو حق الله تعالى أو حق العامة ؟ فقيل بالأول لأن الكفار لما استنكفوا عن عبادته جعلهم الله أرقاء لعباده فكان سبب رقهم كفرهم أو كفر أصولهم، وقيل بالثاني لكونه وسيلة إلى نفعهم وإقامة مصالحهم ودفع الشر عنهم قالوا أول ما يؤخذ المأسور يوصف بالرق ولا يوصف بالملك إلا بعد الإخراج إلى دار الإسلام والملك يوجد في الجماد والحيوان غير الآدمي، دون الرق، وبالبيع يزول ملكه دون الرق. وبالعتق يزول ملكه قصداً لأنه حقه ويزول الرق ضمناً ضرورة فراغه عن حقوق العباد ويتبين لك الفرق بينهما في القن وأم الولد والمكاتب فإن الملك والرق كاملان في القن ورق أم الولد والمدبر ناقص حتى لا يجوز عتقها عن الكفارة والملك فيها كامل حتى جاز وطء أم الولد والمدبرة، والمكاتب رقه كامل حتى جاز عتقه عن الكفارة وملكه ناقص حتى خرج من يد المولى، ولا يدخل تحت قوله «كل مملوك أملكه فهو حر فحاصله أن جواز البيع يعتمد كمالهما، وحل الوطء يعتمد كمال الملك فقط، وجواز العتق عن الكفارة يعتمد كمال الرق فقط . وقيد بالتبعية فيما ذكر للاحتراز عن النسب فإنه للأب لأن النسب للتعريف وحال الرجال مكشوفة دون النساء حتى لو تزوج هاشمي أمة إنسان فأتى بولد فهو هاشمي تبعاً لأبيه رقيق تبعاً لأمه كما في فتح القدير، لأن الزوج قد رضي برق الولد حيث أقدم على تزوجها مع العلم برقها بخلاف المغرور فإن ولده من الأمة حر لأنه لم يرض به لعدم علمه فانعلق حراً وجبت القيمة، وهو ما يستثنى من كلام المصنف فإنه لم يتبع أمه في الرق والملك. وإنما لم يذكره هنا لأنه سيصرح في باب دعوة النسب وللاحتراز عن الدين فإنه يتبع خير الأبوين ديناً لأنه أنظر له .
And the author indicated by joining 'raqq' to 'milk' the difference between them, and it is that milk is the ability to dispose initially, so the guardian, executor, and agent are excluded; as for raqq, it is a legal incapacity for guardianship, testimony, judgment, and ownership of property, arising from its being made by law subject to ownership and subjugation. And they differed whether it is a right of Allah or a right of the public? Some said the first because when the disbelievers refused to worship Him, Allah made them slaves to His servants, so the cause of their slavery was their disbelief or the disbelief of their ancestors. Others said the second because it is a means to benefit them and establish their interests and repel evil from them. They said: first, when a captive is taken, he is described as having raqq but not as having milk until after being brought to the abode of Islam; milk exists in inanimate objects and non-human animals, but raqq does not; by sale, his milk is removed but not his raqq; by emancipation, his milk is removed intentionally because it is his right, and his raqq is removed implicitly due to its becoming empty of the rights of people. And the difference between them becomes clear to you in the qinn, umm walad, and mukatab: indeed milk and raqq are both complete in the qinn; the raqq of the umm walad and mudabbar is deficient so it is not permissible to emancipate her for expiation, while her milk is complete so intercourse with umm walad and mudabbar is permissible; the mukatab's raqq is complete so his emancipation for expiation is permissible, while his milk is deficient until he leaves the hand of the master. And it does not fall under his saying 'every slave that I own is free'. The summary is that the permissibility of sale depends on the completeness of both, the permissibility of intercourse depends on completeness of milk only, and the permissibility of emancipation for expiation depends on completeness of raqq only. And he restricted by dependency in what was mentioned to avoid [confusion with] lineage, for it belongs to the father because lineage is for identification and the condition of men is exposed unlike women, so if a Hashimi marries the female slave of a person and produces a child, he is a Hashimi following his father, a slave following his mother, as in Fath al-Qadir, because the husband has consented to the slavery of the child when he proceeded to marry her with knowledge of her slavery, unlike the deceived [mgharrar], for his child from the female slave is free because he did not consent due to his ignorance, so it was conceived free and its value is due, and this is an exception from the author's statement, for he did not follow his mother in raqq and milk. And he did not mention it here because he will clarify in the chapter on da'wa al-nasab, and to avoid [confusion with] religion, for it follows the better of the two parents in religion because it is more beneficial for him.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling on the distinction between raqq (legal slavery) and milk (ownership). The author of al-Hidayah (or the sharh) explains that milk is the power to dispose, while raqq is a legal incapacity. A key point is that raqq is a right of Allah (according to one view) because it stems from disbelief, or a right of the public (according to another) because it serves societal interests. The passage then illustrates the practical differences through the categories of slaves: qinn (full slave) has both milk and raqq complete; umm walad and mudabbar have deficient raqq but complete milk (so they cannot be used for expiation but intercourse is allowed); mukatab has complete raqq but deficient milk (so can be used for expiation but not fully owned). The passage also clarifies that lineage follows the father, but slavery follows the mother, with the exception of the mugharrar (deceived husband) whose child is free. This distinction is crucial for understanding slave categories and their legal implications.

Key Terms
الرق (al-raqq): A legal incapacity that prevents a person from exercising guardianship, testimony, judgment, and full ownership of property; it is a status created by law.
الملك (al-milk): The power to dispose of property initially; it is the right of ownership that can be transferred.
القن (al-qinn): A full slave who is completely owned and has no right to freedom; both milk and raqq are complete.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has borne a child to her master; her raqq is deficient and she cannot be sold.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which action requires completeness of both milk and raqq?
A) Intercourse
B) Emancipation for expiation
C) Sale
D) Emancipation in general

Key Takeaway
Raqq and milk are distinct legal attributes; their combination determines the permissibility of major actions like sale, intercourse, and expiation.

The Child of a Man from His Own Slave Woman Is Free
States the ruling with proof and reasoning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling regarding the child of a man from his own slave woman and explain the dalil and reasoning that support it.

Core Idea
The child of a man from his own slave woman is free from conception because the father's free fluid prevails.

Islamic law considers the child's status based on the parents' statuses. A key Hanafi ruling is that when a man has a child with his own female slave, the child is born free. This lesson examines the evidence for this ruling, including the example of Ibrahim, the Prophet's son from his slave woman Mariyah, and the legal reasoning that the father's free status overcomes the mother's slave status due to unified ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Primary Ruling
The passage begins by stating: 'And the child of the female slave from her master is free.' This is the clear Hanafi position. Note that the child is free from the moment of conception, not requiring emancipation.
2
Examine the Dalil: The Example of Ibrahim
The author cites a definitive proof: Ibrahim, the son of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), was born from the Prophet's slave woman (Mariyah) and was never anything but free. This historical case demonstrates that a child of a master from his own slave woman is free.
The dalil is a historical precedent (Sunnah in practice) rather than a specific hadith text.
3
Understand the Legal Reasoning (Ta'lil)
The text from al-Mabsut explains the reasoning: the child is conceived from two fluids (sperm and ovum). The father's fluid is free, and the mother's fluid is owned by the father (since she is his slave). Because both fluids belong to the same owner, there is no conflict; the father's free status determines the child's status. Contrast this with a child from another man's slave woman, where the mother's fluid is owned by a different person, creating a conflict that results in the child being a slave unless the father acknowledges him.
4
Note an Exception from Jami' al-Fusulayn
The passage also mentions a scenario where a child can be free from two slave parents without emancipation or bequest. This occurs when a free man has a son from a free woman, then the father marries his own slave woman to that son with the master's consent, and she gives birth. In that case, the child is free because the father (the son) is himself the child of the master, and the mother is the master's slave, so the ownership relationship again results in the child's freedom.
This reinforces the principle that the child's freedom depends on the father being free and the mother being owned by the father.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وولد الأمة من سيدها (حر) لأنه انعلق حراً للقطع بأن إبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن قط إلا حراً إلا أنه يعلق مملوكاً ثم يعتق عليه كما هو ظاهر الهداية وغيرها. وفي المبسوط : الولد يعلق حراً من الماءين لأن ماءه حر وماء جاريته مملوك لسيدها فلا تتحقق المعارضة بخلاف ابنه من جارية الغير فإن ماءها مملوك لغيره فتتحقق المعارضة فيترجح جانبها بأنه مخلوق من مائها بيقين كما قدمناه وسيأتي أنه لا بد أن يعترف به، وفي آخر جامع الفصولين : قد يكون الولد حراً من زوجين رقيقين بلا تحرير ووصية وصورته أن يكون للحر ولد وهو من لأجنبي فزوج الأب أمته من ولده برضا مولاه فولدت الأمة ولداً فهو ولد ولد المولى اهـ. فعلى هذا ولد الأمة من سيدها أو ابن سيدها أو أبي سيدها حر وقد قدمناه أيضاً عن الظهيرية والله أعلم .
His saying: (And the child of the female slave from her master is free) because he is conceived free, definitively as Ibrahim the son of the Prophet (peace be upon him) was never anything but free, except that he is conceived as a slave and then emancipated by him, as is apparent from al-Hidayah and others. And in al-Mabsut: The child is conceived free from two fluids because his fluid is free and the fluid of his female slave is owned by her master, so no conflict arises, unlike his son from the female slave of another, for her fluid is owned by another, so conflict arises, and her side is given preponderance because he is created from her fluid with certainty, as we have presented, and it will come that he must acknowledge him. In the last part of Jami' al-Fusulayn: The child may be free from two slave parents without emancipation and will, and its form is that a free man has a son who is from a foreigner, then the father marries his female slave to his son with the consent of his master, and the female slave gives birth to a child, then he is the child of the child of the master. Thus, the child of the female slave from her master or her master's son or her master's father is free, and we have already presented it from al-Zahiriyya, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof that the child born to a man from his own slave woman is free. The proof is from the example of Ibrahim, the son of the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him), who was born from the Prophet's slave woman and was free. The text distinguishes between two scenarios: when the child is from the man's own slave woman, there is no conflict because the father's free fluid and the mother's slave fluid are both under the same ownership, so the father's freedom prevails. But if the child is from another person's slave woman, the mother's fluid is owned by another, creating a conflict, and the mother's side is given preponderance because the child is certainly created from her fluid; in that case the child is a slave unless the father acknowledges it and pays compensation. The passage also repeats the earlier mentioned case from Jami' al-Fusulayn where a child can be free from two slave parents under specific conditions (when the father himself is a child of the master, and the mother is the master's slave).

Key Terms
ولد الأمة من سيدها (walad al-amah min sayyidiha): The child born to a man from his own female slave; such a child is free according to Hanafi law.
الماء (al-ma'): Here, 'fluid' referring to the semen of the father and the ovum/fluid of the mother in the context of conception.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because the father can emancipate the child after birth.
B) Because the child follows the father's status as a free man.
C) Because the child is conceived free, as both fluids are under the father's ownership, and the example of Ibrahim proves it.
D) Because the mother is a slave, so the child is born a slave but automatically freed.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, a man's child with his own slave woman is free from conception due to the unified ownership of the parents' reproductive fluids.

Hanafi Ruling on Hybrid Animals for Sacrifice
Inter-madhhab dispute on hybrid sacrificial animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sacrificing hybrid animals and explain the difference of opinion between the majority and Imam al-Isbahani.

Core Idea
Hybrid offspring take the ruling of the mother; a dog-sheep hybrid is impermissible for sacrifice according to the majority, but some permit it if it resembles the sheep.

The permissibility of sacrificing hybrid animals for Eid al-Adha depends on the mother's species and the offspring's resemblance. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents examples and a key dispute: while most scholars disallow a hybrid from a dog and a sheep, Imam al-Isbahani allows it if the offspring looks like the mother. Understanding this ruling clarifies the Hanafi stance on mixed-species animals in sacrifice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The passage begins with the rule that the offspring is considered by itself, but examples show it follows the mother's species.
The text 'يعتبر بنفسه' suggests the offspring's own nature determines the ruling, but the examples clarify that the mother's species is decisive.
2
Apply to pure-species hybrid: deer and sheep
A deer mating with a domestic sheep: if the offspring is a sheep, sacrifice is valid; if it is a deer, it is not.
3
Apply to cross-genus hybrid: horse and donkey
A mare giving birth to a donkey: not permissible for sacrifice or consumption.
4
Examine the disputed case: dog and sheep
The majority of scholars (including Hanafis) say it is not permissible; Imam al-Isbahani allows if it resembles the mother.
The majority view is presented first, indicating it is the stronger position.
5
Determine the practical effect (thamarah al-khilaf)
If the offspring resembles a sheep, some scholars permit sacrifice; under the majority view, it is always impermissible regardless of resemblance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحل . وقيل يعتبر بنفسه فيهما حتى إذا نزا ظبي على شاة أهلية فإن ولدت شاة تجوز التضحية بها، وإن ولدت ظبياً لم تجز. ولو ولدت الرمكة حماراً لم يجز ولم يؤكل . وفي الخلاصة في الأضحية المتولدة بين الكلب والشاة قال عامة العلماء : لا يجوز وقال الإمام الحراحاني : إن كان يشبه الأم يجوز اهـ. قوله : (وقدمناه أيضاً عن الظهيرية أي قدم ما نقله عن جامع الفصولين وقدم ذلك قبل ورقة .
And the solution? And it was said: it is considered by itself in both, so if a deer mounts a domestic sheep and it gives birth to a sheep, it is permissible to sacrifice with it, but if it gives birth to a deer, it is not permissible. And if a mare gives birth to a donkey, it is not permissible and not eaten. And in al-Khulasa, regarding the sacrificial animal born between a dog and a sheep: the majority of scholars said it is not permissible, and Imam al-Isbahani (or al-?ar?ani) said: if it resembles the mother, it is permissible. His saying: (And we have also presented it from al-Zahiriyya), i.e., he presented what he transmitted from Jami' al-Fusulayn, and he presented that before the folio.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on hybrid animals for udhiyah (sacrifice). It begins with a statement (perhaps continuing from a previous discussion) that the consideration is based on the animal itself. Then it gives examples: if a deer mates with a domestic sheep, the offspring takes the mother's species; if it looks like a sheep, it is permissible to sacrifice; if like a deer, not. Similarly, if a horse (mare) gives birth to a donkey (from a donkey father), the offspring is not permissible for sacrifice or consumption. Then it mentions a dispute between the majority of scholars and Imam al-Isbahani regarding a hybrid between a dog and a sheep: the majority say it is not permissible, while al-Isbahani says if it resembles the mother, it is permissible. The passage ends with a reference to earlier transmission from al-Zahiriyya and Jami' al-Fusulayn.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-uḍḥiyyah): The sacrificial animal offered during Eid al-Adha.
المتولد (al-mutawallid): A hybrid animal born from two different species.
الرمكة (al-ramakah): A mare (female horse).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is permissible if it resembles the mother.
B) It is permissible if it resembles the father.
C) It is not permissible.
D) It is permissible regardless of resemblance.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a hybrid born from a dog and a sheep cannot be used for sacrifice, even if it resembles the sheep, following the majority position.

The Nature of Slavery (Riqq) and Ownership (Milk) in Hanafi Fiqh
Explaining the nature of slavery and ownership and their application to slave categories.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between riqq and milk, and classify slave categories by the completeness of each status.

Core Idea
Riqq is a legal status specific to humans; milk is ownership applicable to property; their completeness varies by slave type.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies the foundational distinction between two concepts often conflated: riqq (slavery as a legal status) and milk (ownership). The author, using examples from classical Hanafi law, shows how these concepts apply differently to various types of slaves. Understanding this distinction is essential for correctly applying rules of sale, manumission, and expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core definitions
From the passage, note that riqq is a relation of dominion caused by disbelief, while milk is ownership that can exist over non-humans.
2
Distinguish riqq from milk
Sale removes milk but not riqq; manumission removes both but with different intentionality. Milk can be found in animals and objects, riqq only in humans.
This is the key distinction.
3
Classify slave categories
List qinn, umm walad, mudabbar, mukatab. Determine completeness of riqq and milk for each as stated in the passage.
Refer to the text: qinn both complete; umm walad: riqq incomplete, milk complete; mukatab: riqq complete, milk incomplete.
4
Apply the effects
Based on completeness, deduce legal consequences: sale requires both complete; intercourse requires only milk complete; expiatory manumission requires riqq complete.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب العتق
عبادته جعلهم الله أرقاء لعباده فكان سبب رقهم كفرهم أو كفر أصولهم، وقيل بالثاني لكونه وسيلة إلى نفعهم وإقامة مصالحهم ودفع الشر عنهم قالوا أول ما يؤخذ المأسور يوصف بالرق ولا يوصف بالملك إلا بعد الإخراج إلى دار الإسلام والملك يوجد في الجماد والحيوان غير الآدمي، دون الرق، وبالبيع يزول ملكه دون الرق. وبالعتق يزول ملكه قصداً لأنه حقه ويزول الرق ضمناً ضرورة فراغه عن حقوق العباد ويتبين لك الفرق بينهما في القن وأم الولد والمكاتب فإن الملك والرق كاملان في القن ورق أم الولد والمدبر ناقص حتى لا يجوز عتقها عن الكفارة والملك فيها كامل حتى جاز وطء أم الولد والمدبرة، والمكاتب رقه كامل حتى جاز عتقه عن الكفارة وملكه ناقص حتى خرج من يد المولى، ولا يدخل تحت قوله «كل مملوك أملكه فهو حر فحاصله أن جواز البيع يعتمد كمالهما، وحل الوطء يعتمد كمال الملك فقط، وجواز العتق عن الكفارة يعتمد كمال الرق فقط . وقيد بالتبعية فيما ذكر للاحتراز عن النسب فإنه للأب لأن النسب للتعريف وحال الرجال مكشوفة دون النساء حتى لو تزوج هاشمي أمة إنسان فأتى بولد فهو هاشمي تبعاً لأبيه رقيق تبعاً لأمه كما في فتح القدير، لأن الزوج قد رضي برق الولد حيث أقدم على تزوجها مع العلم برقها بخلاف المغرور فإن ولده من الأمة حر لأنه لم يرض به لعدم علمه فانعلق حراً وجبت القيمة، وهو ما يستثنى من كلام المصنف فإنه لم يتبع أمه في الرق والملك. وإنما لم يذكره هنا لأنه سيصرح في باب دعوة النسب وللاحتراز عن الدين فإنه يتبع خير الأبوين ديناً لأنه أنظر له . قوله : (وولد الأمة من سيدها (حر) لأنه انعلق حراً للقطع بأن إبراهيم ابن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لم يكن قط إلا حراً إلا أنه يعلق مملوكاً ثم يعتق عليه كما هو ظاهر الهداية وغيرها. وفي المبسوط : الولد يعلق حراً من الماءين لأن ماءه حر وماء جاريته مملوك لسيدها فلا تتحقق المعارضة بخلاف ابنه من جارية الغير فإن ماءها مملوك لغيره فتتحقق المعارضة فيترجح جانبها بأنه مخلوق من مائها بيقين كما قدمناه وسيأتي أنه لا بد أن يعترف به، وفي آخر جامع الفصولين : قد يكون الولد حراً من زوجين رقيقين بلا تحرير ووصية وصورته أن يكون للحر ولد وهو من لأجنبي فزوج الأب أمته من ولده برضا مولاه فولدت الأمة ولداً فهو ولد ولد المولى اهـ. فعلى هذا ولد الأمة من سيدها أو ابن سيدها أو أبي سيدها حر وقد قدمناه أيضاً عن الظهيرية والله أعلم .
Book of Manumission. His worship: Allah made them slaves to His servants, so the cause of their slavery is their disbelief or the disbelief of their ancestors, and it is said by the second because it is a means to benefit them, manage their interests, and repel evil from them. They said: When the captive is first taken, he is described with slavery (riqq) and is not described with ownership (milk) except after being brought out to the abode of Islam. Ownership is found in inanimate objects and non-human animals, but not slavery. By sale, his ownership is removed without his slavery. By manumission, his ownership is removed intentionally because it is his right, and slavery is removed implicitly due to necessity of vacating the rights of servants. The difference between them is made clear in the case of a qinn, umm walad, and mukatab: for ownership and slavery are complete in the qinn; the slavery of umm walad and mudabbar is incomplete such that their manumission is not valid for expiation, while ownership in them is complete, so intercourse with umm walad and mudabbarah is permissible. The mukatab: his slavery is complete such that his manumission is valid for expiation, and his ownership is incomplete such that he leaves the hand of the master, and he does not enter under his statement: 'Every slave I own is free.' So the gist is that the permissibility of sale depends on their completeness, the permissibility of intercourse depends only on completeness of ownership, and the permissibility of manumission for expiation depends only on completeness of slavery. The restriction to followership in what was mentioned is to avoid lineage, for it belongs to the father because lineage is for identification, and the condition of men is open unlike women. So if a Hashimi marries the female slave of a person and she gives birth to a child, the child is Hashimi following his father and a slave following his mother, as in Fath al-Qadir, because the husband consented to the child's slavery by proceeding to marry her knowing her slavery, unlike the deceived one (maghrur), for his child from the female slave is free because he did not consent due to lack of knowledge, so it clings free and the price is owed, and this is what is excluded from the author's statement, for he did not follow his mother in slavery and ownership. He did not mention it here because he will clarify in the chapter on claims of lineage. And to avoid the matter of religion, for it follows the better of the two parents in religion because it is more beneficial for him. His statement: 'The child of a female slave by her master is free' because he clings free as it is definitive that Ibrahim, son of the Prophet (peace be upon him), was never anything but free, except that he clings as a slave and then is freed upon him, as is apparent in al-Hidayah and others. In al-Mabsut: The child clings free from the two waters because his water is free and the water of his female slave is owned by her master, so there is no conflict, unlike his child from the female slave of another, for her water is owned by someone else, so conflict arises, and her side is given preponderance because he is created from her water with certainty, as we have mentioned, and it will come that he must acknowledge him. In the last part of Jami' al-Fusulain: The child may be free from two slave spouses without manumission or will. Its form is that a free man has a son who is a stranger, so he marries his female slave to his own son with the permission of her master, then the female slave gives birth to a child, so the child is the child of the son of the master. End quote. According to this, the child of a female slave by her master, or by the son of her master, or by the father of her master, is free, and we have also mentioned it from al-Zahiriyya, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling discussion on the nature of slavery (riqq) and ownership (milk) in Hanafi fiqh. The author explains that slavery is a legal status caused by disbelief (kufr) of the slave or their ancestors, and it is a means for the master's benefit and maintenance of order. The primary distinction: ownership (milk) can be found in inanimate objects and animals, while slavery is specific to human beings. Sale removes ownership but not slavery; manumission ('itq) removes ownership intentionally and slavery implicitly. The difference manifests in three categories: (1) qinn (full slave) has complete slavery and ownership; (2) umm walad (mother of master's child) and mudabbar (slave promised freedom after master's death) have incomplete slavery (cannot be used for expiatory manumission) but complete ownership (master may have intercourse); (3) mukatab (slave who contracts to purchase freedom) has complete slavery (valid for expiation) but incomplete ownership (master's ownership is suspended). The discussion also covers lineage: a child follows the better-dined parent in religion, but in slavery, the child of a Hashimi man from a female slave is free following the father? Actually it says the child is a slave following the mother unless the father was unaware of her slavery (maghrur), in which case the child is free and the master must pay the value. The child of a female slave by her owner is free from the moment of conception because the master's water is free. Special cases include a child from two slave spouses with a complex scenario. The author concludes by referencing previous mention from al-Zahiriyya.

Key Terms
الرق (al-riqq): The legal status of being a slave; a relation of dominion between master and slave that is a consequence of disbelief or captivity.
الملك (al-milk): Ownership; a legal right over something that can be transferred by sale or manumission.
القن (al-qinn): A fully-owned slave (not a mudabbar, mukatab, or umm walad) with complete slavery and ownership.
أم الولد (umm al-walad): A female slave who has given birth to her master's child; her slavery is incomplete (cannot be sold or used for expiation), but she is not fully free until master's death.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave who enters a contract of kitaba with the master to purchase his freedom by paying installments; his slavery is complete until full payment.
المدبر (al-mudabbar): A slave whom the master has promised to free after his death; the slave's slavery is incomplete during the master's lifetime.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which category of slave has complete slavery such that manumission is valid for expiation?
A) Umm walad
B) Mudabbar
C) Mukatab
D) Qinn

Key Takeaway
Understanding the distinction between riqq and milk and their completeness in different slave categories is essential for correctly applying Hanafi rulings on sale, manumission, and expiation.

Sacrifice of Hybrid Animals: Resemblance to Mother Decides
Ruling on sacrifice of hybrid animals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on sacrificing hybrid animals and apply the principle that offspring follows the mother's species in determining validity.

Core Idea
A hybrid animal is valid for sacrifice only if it resembles a permissible mother species.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a niche but important question: when two animals of different species crossbreed, can their offspring be used for udhiya? The answer hinges on resemblance to the mother. The text gives concrete examples (gazelle-sheep, horse-donkey) and notes a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars (Imam al-Karkhi's view). Understanding this ruling clarifies the general principle that the offspring's legal status follows the mother in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its General Ruling
The act under discussion is the sacrifice (udhiya) of a hybrid animal (mutawallid bayna naw'ayn). Identify the default ruling: most scholars say it is not permissible unless it resembles the mother of a permissible species.
2
Analyze the Examples Given
Two examples are provided: (1) a gazelle mounts a domestic sheep – if the offspring is a sheep, it is valid; if a gazelle, invalid. (2) A female horse gives birth to a donkey (mule) – not permissible and not eaten. These illustrate the rule.
The offspring's appearance determines the ruling.
3
Locate the Proof (Dalil) and Its Application
The proof is based on qiyas (analogy) using the principle that offspring follows the mother (al-walad yatba'u al-umm). For sacrifice, the animal must be from a permissible species (sheep, goat, cow, camel). If the mother is permissible, and the offspring resembles her, it is valid; otherwise not.
This is a zanni (probable) dalil, as it involves reasoning.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Imam al-Karkhi (a Hanafi scholar) differs: if the hybrid resembles the mother, it is allowed even if the father is from a non-permissible species. The majority (including the author) side with the stricter view that it must actually be of the mother's species, not just resemble.
The mufta bihi (operative view) is the majority position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والحل . وقيل يعتبر بنفسه فيهما حتى إذا نزا ظبي على شاة أهلية فإن ولدت شاة تجوز التضحية بها، وإن ولدت ظبياً لم تجز. ولو ولدت الرمكة حماراً لم يجز ولم يؤكل . وفي الخلاصة في الأضحية المتولدة بين الكلب والشاة قال عامة العلماء : لا يجوز وقال الإمام الحراحاني : إن كان يشبه الأم يجوز اهـ.
And the solution. It is said that it is considered by itself in both such that when a gazelle mounts a domestic sheep, if the sheep gives birth to a sheep, sacrificing it is permissible, but if it gives birth to a gazelle, it is not permissible. And if a female horse gives birth to a donkey, it is not permissible and not eaten. And in al-Khulasa concerning the hybrid between a dog and a sheep, the generality of scholars said: it is not permissible, and Imam al-Karkhi said: if it resembles the mother, it is permissible. End quote.
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage presents rulings on the sacrifice (udhiya) of hybrid animals. The general principle is that the offspring follows the mother's species in determining permissibility for sacrifice. If a gazelle mounts a domestic sheep, and the offspring resembles a sheep, sacrifice is valid; if it resembles a gazelle (wild), it is not. Similarly, a mule (from horse and donkey) cannot be sacrificed or eaten. The author cites a dispute from al-Khulasa about a dog-sheep hybrid: most scholars forbid it, but Imam al-Karkhi allows it if the offspring resembles the mother (sheep). This is consistent with the Hanafi reliance on istihsan and consideration of dominant resemblance.

Key Terms
الأضحية (al-udhiya): The sacrifice of an animal during the days of Eid al-Adha; specific conditions apply to the animal.
المتولد بين نوعين (al-mutawallid bayna naw'ayn): A hybrid animal resulting from crossbreeding of two different species.
شبه الأم (shabah al-umm): Resemblance to the mother; used as a criterion by Imam al-Karkhi for permissibility.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is permissible because the mother is a horse.

Key Takeaway
A hybrid animal is valid for udhiya only if it actually belongs to a permissible species, determined by the mother's species, not merely by resemblance.

Partial Manumission: Abu Hanifa vs Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on partial manumission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on partial manumission and explain the practical difference (thamarah al-khilaf) between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
Partial manumission frees only the freed portion; the slave works for the rest – but Sahibayn say the whole slave is freed.

This passage addresses a classic intra-Hanafi dispute: if a master frees part of his slave, does the slave become fully free or only partly? Abu Hanifa holds that only the freed portion is free, and the slave must earn the remainder, like a mukatab. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) argue that the whole slave is freed because manumission is indivisible. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a difference in legal theory (divisibility of manumission) leads to different rulings.

Guided Path
1
State Abu Hanifa's ruling
Read the opening line: 'Whoever frees a part of his slave, the slave is not fully freed, and he works for the remainder.' This is Abu Hanifa's view.
The phrase 'like a mukatab' indicates the slave works to earn his freedom.
2
State the Sahibayn's ruling
Immediately after, the text says 'And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is fully freed.' This is the opposing view.
Sahibayn hold that the whole slave is freed regardless of the portion freed.
3
Identify the proofs
The text provides a rational argument: a person's disposal is confined to his own right (ownership), not slavery (which is a right of Allah). Scriptural evidence from a hadith in the Sahihayn about freeing one's share.
The hadith is cut off but indicates valuation and working off.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Under Abu Hanifa, the slave remains partly enslaved and must work (sa'y) to earn the remaining portion. Under Sahibayn, the slave is fully free and the master must compensate co-owners if any.
This practical consequence is decisive for application.
5
Identify the mufta bihi
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view as the chapter's ruling and the Sahibayn's as a counterview. Later Hanafi authorities (e.g., al-Hidayah) prefer Abu Hanifa's position.
The operative ruling for fatwa is that of Abu Hanifa.

قوله : (فالحق إن الخيارات خمسة بل ستة بزيادة الصلح المذكور عن البدائع آنفاً .
Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. Whoever frees a part of his slave, the slave is not fully freed, and he works for the remainder, and he is like a mukatab. And if he frees... Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. There is no doubt about the frequent occurrence of full manumission and the rarity of partial manumission, and that what is frequent is more in need of explanation than what is rare, and that meeting urgent need takes precedence over the rare. Therefore he delayed this chapter after the previous one. His statement: 'Whoever frees a part of his slave, he is not fully freed, and he works for the remainder, and he is like a mukatab.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is fully freed. The mashayikh differed in framing the point of dispute. The author of al-Hidayah and many held that it is based on whether manumission (‘itq) is divisible (yutajazza’) according to him, so it is limited to what he freed, while according to them it is not divisible. And evidence was adduced from both sides. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the intended meaning of divisibility of manumission and ownership is that the subject (the slave) is divisible in receiving the ruling of manumission (removal of ownership) such that ownership may be removed from part and not from another, and that the subject is divisible in receiving the ruling of ownership such that part may be owned by one and part by another. It does not mean that the essence of manumission or ownership is divisible because its meaning is unitary and does not accept division. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: What consideration demands is that this is a mistake in framing the dispute, for they did not address a single issue regarding divisibility. The one who says that manumission or freeing is divisible does not mean it in the sense that the one who says it is not divisible means (i.e., removal of slavery or its abolition), for there is no disagreement among them about its non-divisibility. Rather, removal of ownership and its abolition: there is no disagreement about its divisibility. So it should not be said that they differed about divisibility of manumission or freeing. Rather, the dispute is really only about what manumission necessitates primarily and essentially. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is removal of ownership, and removal of slavery follows it, so the divisibility of its consequence (the removal of ownership) is necessary. However, removal of slavery is not established except when ownership is removed from the entirety legally, by analogy to the minor impurity (hadath) which is only removed when all limbs are washed, and washing them is divisible. This is because manumission is a religious empowerment (quwwa shar‘iyya) that grants ability to perform religiously valid transactions, and it is inconceivable to establish this in part of him as a share. So it is definitively judged that removal of ownership from part does not occur, and removal of slavery is suspended on its divisibility. Ownership is divisible, so what we said about removal of ownership from the remainder follows. In that case, evidence should be presented from both sides on whether what is primarily established is removal of ownership or removal of slavery, for that is the point of dispute, and the argument for Abu Hanifa is strong. As for the rational argument: a person's disposal (tasarruf) is confined to his right, and his right is ownership. As for slavery, it is a right of Allah or a public right. As for scriptural evidence: in the two Sahihs, raised to the Prophet: 'Whoever frees his share in a slave and has wealth sufficient to cover the price of the slave, the slave is valued against him...' (cut off). Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. His statement: (The correct view is that there are five options, rather six with the addition of the reconciliation mentioned earlier from al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding partial manumission of a slave. The basic ruling: if someone frees a portion of his slave, according to Abu Hanifa, only that portion becomes free, and the slave must work to earn his remaining freedom (like a mukatab). According to the Sahibayn, the entire slave becomes free, and the master must compensate the other co-owners if any. The author then reports a discussion among later scholars about the precise nature of the disagreement. Some, like the author of al-Hidayah, say it is about whether the act of manumission is divisible (tajazzu’). Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible, so only the freed portion is affected; the Sahibayn hold it is not divisible, so the whole is freed. Others, like the author of Fath al-Qadir, critique this framing, arguing that both sides agree that the removal of slavery (zawal al-riqq) is not divisible, but they differ on what manumission primarily causes: Abu Hanifa says it is removal of ownership (zawal al-milk), which is divisible, and removal of slavery follows only when ownership is fully removed. The Sahibayn say manumission primarily causes removal of slavery directly, which is indivisible, so the whole slave is freed. The text then provides a rational argument (ma‘na) and scriptural evidence (sam‘) from a hadith in the Sahihayn. The passage ends with a fragment mentioning 'five options' which seems to be a separate topic.

Key Terms
التجزي (al-tajazzu'): Divisibility; whether a legal act or status can be divided into parts. Here used for the act of manumission and the removal of ownership/slavery.
السعي (al-sa'y): The effort/work the partially freed slave performs to earn money to pay for his remaining portion of freedom.
المكاتب (al-mukatab): A slave under contract of kitaba to purchase freedom; the partially freed slave is analogous to him because he works to buy his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Abu Hanifa says the slave is freed; Sahibayn say he is not.
B) Abu Hanifa says the slave works for the remainder; Sahibayn say the master must compensate.
C) Both agree the slave is fully freed.
D) Abu Hanifa says the manumission is invalid; Sahibayn say it is valid.

Key Takeaway
Partial manumission is valid per Abu Hanifa (mufta bihi), with the slave working for the remainder, while the Sahibayn hold the whole slave is freed and the master compensates.

The Real Point of Dispute: Methodological Refinement
Methodological refinement of the dispute's framing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct framing of the dispute between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on partial manumission, distinguishing the earlier mistaken framing from the refined one.

Core Idea
The real dispute is not about divisibility of manumission, but about its primary effect: removal of ownership or removal of slavery.

This lesson unpacks a methodological critique within the Hanafi school. Later scholars like the author of Fath al-Qadir pointed out that earlier scholars (e.g., al-Hidayah) misidentified the point of disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn. Instead of debating whether manumission itself is divisible, the true dispute is about what manumission primarily causes: removal of ownership (divisible) or removal of slavery (indivisible). Understanding such refinements sharpens your ability to engage with scholarly ikhtilaf critically.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earlier framing
Read the part where the author of al-Hidayah states that the dispute is about whether manumission (i'taq) is divisible (tajazzu').
This framing says Abu Hanifa holds divisibility and Sahibayn hold non-divisibility.
2
Understand the critique from Fath al-Qadir
The author argues this is a mistake (ghalat). He points out that both sides agree that removal of slavery is indivisible and removal of ownership is divisible.
Thus, the dispute cannot be about divisibility per se.
3
Identify the correct point of dispute
The real dispute is: what does manumission necessitate first and primarily (awwalan wa bi al-dhat)? Abu Hanifa: removal of ownership. Sahibayn: removal of slavery.
This determines whether the effect is divisible (ownership) or not (slavery).
4
Follow the consequence
If the primary effect is removal of ownership (divisible), then partial manumission frees only that portion. If primary effect is removal of slavery (indivisible), then the whole slave is freed.
The ruling follows from this foundational difference.
5
Appreciate the value of the refinement
This critique shows how later scholars (mutakhkhirin) refine the understanding of earlier authorities (mutaqaddimin), ensuring precision in legal theory.
Such critical refinement is part of the usul al-fiqh and iftaa tradition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب العبد يعتق بعضه
من أعتق بعض عبده لم يعتق كله وسعى فيما بقي وهو كالمكاتب وإن أعتق
باب العبد يعتق بعضه
لا شك في كثرة وقوع عتق الكل وندرة عتق البعض وفي أن ما كثر وجوده فالحاجة إلى بيان أحكامه أمس منها إلى ما يندر وجوده، وأن دفع الحاجة الماسة تقدم على النادرة فلذا أخر هذا عما قبله قوله : (من أعتق بعض عبده لم يعتق كله وسعى فيما بقي وهو كالمكاتب) وهذا عند أبي حنيفة وقالا يعتق كله واختلف المشايخ في تحرير محل النزاع؛ فذهب صاحب الهداية وكثير إلى أنه مبني على أن الإعتاق يتجزأ عنده فيقتصر على ما أعتق . وعندهما لا يتجزأ وأقام الدليل من الجانبين وفي غاية البيان والمراد من تجزىء الإعتاق والملك أن يتجزأ المحل في قبول حكم الإعتاق وهو زوال الملك بأن يزول في البعض دون البعض وأن يتجزأ المحل في قبول حكم الملك وهو أن يكون البعض مملوكاً لواحد والبعض الآخر لآخر، وليس معناه أن ذات الإعتاق أو ذات الملك تتجزأ لأن معناه واحد لا يقبل التجزي اهـ. وفي فتح القدير : والذي يقتضيه النظر أن هذا غلط في تحرير محل النزاع فإنهم لم يتواردوا على محل واحد في التجزي وعدمه فإن القائل العتق أو الإعتاق يتجزأ لم يرده بالمعنى الذي يريد به قائل أنه لا يتجزأ وهو زوال الرق أو إزالته إذ لا خلاف بينهم في عدم تجزئه، بل زوال الملك وإزالته ولا خلاف في تجزئه فلا ينبغي أن يقال اختلف في تجزئ العتق وعدمه ولا الإعتاق بل الخلاف في التحقيق ليس إلا فيما يوجبه الإعتاق أولاً وبالذات ؛ فعنده زوال الملك ويتبعه زوال الرق فلزم تجزؤ موجبه غير أن زوال الرق لا يثبت إلا عند زوال الملك عن الكل شرعاً لحكم الحدث لا يزول إلا عند غسل كل الأعضاء وغسلها متجزىء، وهذا لضرورة أن العتق قوة شرعية هي قدرة على تصرفات شرعية ولا يتصور ثبوت هذه في بعضه شائعاً فقطع بعدم من زوال الملك عن البعض وتوقف زوال الرق تجزئه، والملك متجزىء فلزم ما قلنا على زوال الملك عن الباقي وحينئذ فينبغي أن يقام الدليل من الجانبين على أن الثابت به أولاً زوال الملك أو الرق لأنه محل النزاع والوجه منتهض لأبي حنيفة. أما المعنى فلأن تصرف الإنسان يقتصر على حقه وحقه الملك وأما الرق فحق الله أو حق العامة، وأما السمع فما في الصحيحين مرفوعاً من أعتق شريكاً له في عبد فكان له مال يبلغ ثمن العبد قوم عليه

قوله : (فالحق إن الخيارات خمسة بل ستة بزيادة الصلح المذكور عن البدائع آنفاً .
Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. Whoever frees a part of his slave, the slave is not fully freed, and he works for the remainder, and he is like a mukatab. And if he frees... Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. There is no doubt about the frequent occurrence of full manumission and the rarity of partial manumission, and that what is frequent is more in need of explanation than what is rare, and that meeting urgent need takes precedence over the rare. Therefore he delayed this chapter after the previous one. His statement: 'Whoever frees a part of his slave, he is not fully freed, and he works for the remainder, and he is like a mukatab.' This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: He is fully freed. The mashayikh differed in framing the point of dispute. The author of al-Hidayah and many held that it is based on whether manumission (‘itq) is divisible (yutajazza’) according to him, so it is limited to what he freed, while according to them it is not divisible. And evidence was adduced from both sides. In Ghayat al-Bayan, the intended meaning of divisibility of manumission and ownership is that the subject (the slave) is divisible in receiving the ruling of manumission (removal of ownership) such that ownership may be removed from part and not from another, and that the subject is divisible in receiving the ruling of ownership such that part may be owned by one and part by another. It does not mean that the essence of manumission or ownership is divisible because its meaning is unitary and does not accept division. End quote. In Fath al-Qadir: What consideration demands is that this is a mistake in framing the dispute, for they did not address a single issue regarding divisibility. The one who says that manumission or freeing is divisible does not mean it in the sense that the one who says it is not divisible means (i.e., removal of slavery or its abolition), for there is no disagreement among them about its non-divisibility. Rather, removal of ownership and its abolition: there is no disagreement about its divisibility. So it should not be said that they differed about divisibility of manumission or freeing. Rather, the dispute is really only about what manumission necessitates primarily and essentially. According to him (Abu Hanifa), it is removal of ownership, and removal of slavery follows it, so the divisibility of its consequence (the removal of ownership) is necessary. However, removal of slavery is not established except when ownership is removed from the entirety legally, by analogy to the minor impurity (hadath) which is only removed when all limbs are washed, and washing them is divisible. This is because manumission is a religious empowerment (quwwa shar‘iyya) that grants ability to perform religiously valid transactions, and it is inconceivable to establish this in part of him as a share. So it is definitively judged that removal of ownership from part does not occur, and removal of slavery is suspended on its divisibility. Ownership is divisible, so what we said about removal of ownership from the remainder follows. In that case, evidence should be presented from both sides on whether what is primarily established is removal of ownership or removal of slavery, for that is the point of dispute, and the argument for Abu Hanifa is strong. As for the rational argument: a person's disposal (tasarruf) is confined to his right, and his right is ownership. As for slavery, it is a right of Allah or a public right. As for scriptural evidence: in the two Sahihs, raised to the Prophet: 'Whoever frees his share in a slave and has wealth sufficient to cover the price of the slave, the slave is valued against him...' (cut off). Chapter on the slave who is partially freed. His statement: (The correct view is that there are five options, rather six with the addition of the reconciliation mentioned earlier from al-Bada'i'.
Source pages p. 395

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding partial manumission of a slave. The basic ruling: if someone frees a portion of his slave, according to Abu Hanifa, only that portion becomes free, and the slave must work to earn his remaining freedom (like a mukatab). According to the Sahibayn, the entire slave becomes free, and the master must compensate the other co-owners if any. The author then reports a discussion among later scholars about the precise nature of the disagreement. Some, like the author of al-Hidayah, say it is about whether the act of manumission is divisible (tajazzu’). Abu Hanifa holds it is divisible, so only the freed portion is affected; the Sahibayn hold it is not divisible, so the whole is freed. Others, like the author of Fath al-Qadir, critique this framing, arguing that both sides agree that the removal of slavery (zawal al-riqq) is not divisible, but they differ on what manumission primarily causes: Abu Hanifa says it is removal of ownership (zawal al-milk), which is divisible, and removal of slavery follows only when ownership is fully removed. The Sahibayn say manumission primarily causes removal of slavery directly, which is indivisible, so the whole slave is freed. The text then provides a rational argument (ma‘na) and scriptural evidence (sam‘) from a hadith in the Sahihayn. The passage ends with a fragment mentioning 'five options' which seems to be a separate topic.

Key Terms
تحرير محل النزاع (tahrir mahall al-niza'): Framing the point of dispute; identifying exactly what the disagreement is about.
الغلط في التحرير (al-ghalat fi al-tahrir): A mistake in framing the dispute; a critique that the issue was not correctly identified.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Fath al-Qadir, why is the earlier framing of the dispute (divisibility of manumission) considered a mistake?
A) Because the earlier scholars misquoted the hadith.
B) Because both sides agree on the divisibility of ownership and indivisibility of slavery, so the dispute must be about the primary effect.
C) Because Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn actually agree on the ruling.
D) Because the Sahibayn changed their positions later.

Key Takeaway
The refined framing of the dispute: the difference is not about divisibility but about the primary effect of manumission (removal of ownership vs. removal of slavery).

Partial Emancipation: Abu Hanifa vs. the Sahibayn
Commentary on partial emancipation with analysis of the intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on partial emancipation, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute, and identify the key rational and transmitted proofs.

Core Idea
Partial emancipation frees only the owner's share; the slave must earn the rest, like a mukatab.

This lesson examines a classic intra-Hanafi dispute regarding partial emancipation. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, if an owner frees part of his slave, the slave does not become fully free; rather, he becomes a mustas'a, obligated to earn the remaining value. The two companions, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, hold that the slave becomes completely free immediately. Understanding the precise nature of this disagreement—whether it hinges on the divisibility of emancipation or on what the act primarily necessitates—is key to grasping Hanafi legal reasoning.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling of Imam Abu Hanifa: the slave is not fully freed; he must earn the remaining portion of his value and is treated like a mukatab (a slave contracting for freedom).
This is the mufta bihi position of the Hanafi school.
2
Identify the opponent's view
State the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani): the slave becomes completely free immediately upon partial emancipation.
They argue that emancipation is indivisible—freeing part frees the whole.
3
Analyse the Hanafi reply to the opponent's proof
Examine Abu Hanifa's rational proof: a person's disposal only affects his own right (ownership), while slavery is a right of Allah or the public, so the act cannot directly eliminate slavery. Then consider the transmitted proof from the hadith: 'Whoever frees his share in a slave...' which conditions full freedom on the owner having sufficient wealth.
The hadith implies that if the owner lacks wealth, only the freed portion is free.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: according to Abu Hanifa, the slave remains partially enslaved and must work to earn his freedom (mustas'a). According to the Sahibayn, the slave is instantly free.
The difference affects the slave's status in matters of earnings, liability, and inheritance.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Understand that the Hanafi school relies on Abu Hanifa's view. The reasoning is that ownership is divisible while the right of slavery is not directly subject to the owner's disposal, supported by the explicit hadith.
The detailed defense in the text indicates this is the mufta bihi.
